                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/sub&gt;/SnS@C hollow hierarchical nanotubes as superior performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Lin-bo; Zhang, Bao; Peng, Tao; He, Zhen-jiang; Yan, Cheng; Mao, Jing; Dai, Kehua; Wu, Xian-wen; Zheng, Jun-chao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">90</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_A</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">106568</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a two-dimensional layered material, SnS is considered a promising candidate anode material for sodium storage due to its high theor. capacity (1022 mA h g-1) and large interlayer spacing (4.33 Å).  However, its application is hindered by its large vol. expansion and low electronic cond.  Herein, a unique MoS2/SnS@C hollow hierarchical nanotube with self-supporting structure was synthesized through a facile solvothermal reaction.  The results indicate that the hollow nanotube structure can support the material structure and provide a large sodium-ion migration channel.  In addn., the heterojunction that formed between SnS and MoS2 can effectively reduce the kinetic barrier of sodium-ion diffusion.  Furthermore, the hollow hierarchical nanotube can effectively alleviate the radial and hoop stresses of the SnS sodiation process, inhibit the vol. expansion of the material, and increase the capacitance contribution ratio of the material at a high rate.  The MoS2/SnS@C composites used as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) delivered excellent rate and cycle performance.  The discharge capacity was about 325 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 15 A g-1, and it remained at about 292 mA h g-1 after 2000 cycles at 5 A g-1 c.d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201401205"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin MoS2 Nanosheets as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Superior Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Dawei; Dou, Shixue; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1401205/1-1401205/6</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Few-layer MoS2 nanosheets are successfully synthesized using a simple and scalable ultrasonic exfoliation technique.  The thicknesses of the MoS2 nanosheets ares about 10 nm as measured by SEM (SEM) and at. force microscopy (AFM).  The unique nanosheet architecture renders the high-rate transportation of sodium ions due to the short diffusion paths provided by ultrathin thickness and the large interlayer space within the MoS2 crystal structure (d(002) = 6.38 Å).  When applied as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, MoS2 nanosheets exhibit a high, reversible sodium storage capacity and excellent cyclability.  The MoS2 nanosheets also demonstrate good electrochem. performance at high current densities.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201407898"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2 Nanoflowers with Expanded Interlayers as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Wang, Lixiu; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Cheng, Fangyi; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayer spacing of the (002) plane were synthesized and used as high-performance anode in Na-ion batteries.  By controlling the cut-off voltage to the range of 0.4-3 V, an intercalation mechanism rather than a conversion reaction is taking place.  The MoS2 nanoflower electrode shows high discharge capacities of 350 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, 300 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 195 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1. The stripping of MoS2 layers occurring in charge/discharge cycling contributes to the enhanced kinetics and low energy barrier for the intercalation of Na+ ions.  The electrochem. reaction is mainly controlled by the capacitive process, which facilitates the high-rate capability.  Therefore, MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers hold promise for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201915917"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X. The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, an electrode has been proposed and designed on its interior structure and controlled morphol., Specifically, metallic WS2 hollow microspheres have been synthesized via a one-step solvothermal process, in the absence of additives, consisting of porous nanosheets with a large surface area.  The individual nanosheet features an expanded interlayer distance of 1.02 nm and metallic characteristics, which can provide faster transport of electrons and reduce the diffusion pathway for sodium ions.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tungsten diselenide nanoplates as advanced lithium/sodium ion electrode materials with different storage mechanisms</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Wanfeng; Wang, Jiawei; Si, Conghui; Peng, Zhangquan; Zhang, Zhonghua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2584-2598</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) exhibit immense potential as lithium/ sodium-ion electrode materials owing to their sandwich-like layered structures.  To optimize their lithium/sodium-storage performance, two issues should be addressed: fundamentally understanding the chem. reaction occurring in TMD electrodes and developing novel TMDs.  In this study, WSe2 hexagonal nanoplates were synthesized as lithium/sodium-ion battery (LIB/SIB) electrode materials.  For LIBs, the WSe2-nanoplate electrodes achieved a stable reversible capacity and a high rate capability, as well as an ultralong cycle life of up to 1,500 cycles at 1,000 mA·g-1.  Most importantly, in situ Raman spectroscopy, ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD), transmission electron microscopy, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy measurements performed during the discharge-charge process clearly verified the reversible conversion mechanism, which can be summarized as follows: WSe2 + 4Li+ + 4e- ↔ W + 2Li2Se.  The WSe2 nanoplates also exhibited excellent cycling performance and a high rate capability as SIB electrodes.  Ex situ XRD and Raman spectroscopy results demonstrate that WSe2 reacted with Na+ more easily and thoroughly than with Li+ and converted to Na2Se and tungsten in the 1st sodiated state.  The subsequent charging reaction can be expressed as Na2Se → Se + 2Na+ + 2e-, which differs from the traditional conversion mechanism for LIBs.  To our knowledge, this is the first systematic exploration of the lithium/sodium-storage performance of WSe2 and the mechanism involved.         </div><div class="casAbstract">From first-principles calcns., we discover highly stable monolayer transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) ternary alloys consisting of group 5 and 7 transition metal elements.  We show for Nb1-xRexS2, Ta1-xRexS2 and their selenide counterparts that the 1H ordered alloy structures for x ≤ 0.5 are thermodynamically stable, with formation energies an order of magnitude lower than currently known TMD alloys such as MoxW1-xS2, so that they could potentially be synthesizable using chem. vapor deposition or exfoliation techniques.  This class of TMD alloys offer a wide tunable bandgap range of ∼1 eV, displaying metallic to semiconducting behavior vs. alloy compn.  Importantly, at x = 0.5, the alloys are valence isoelectronic with MoS2.  These stoichiometric compds., Nb0.5Re0.5S2, Ta0.5Re0.5S2, and their selenide counterparts, exhibit band features similar to MoS2, but possess significantly smaller bandgaps (∼1 to 1.2 eV).  As a result, compared to MoS2 and WS2, this class of alloy TMDs display enhanced absorbance in the visible range of the solar spectrum where the solar spectral intensity is the strongest.  These ordered monolayer TMD alloys could open doors for designing ultrathin solar absorbers with improved performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1021/nl903868w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Splendiani, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chim, C.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Galli, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Emerging Photoluminescence in Monolayer MoS2</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1271</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1275</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel phys. phenomena can emerge in low-dimensional nanomaterials.  Bulk MoS2, a prototypical metal dichalcogenide, is an indirect bandgap semiconductor with negligible photoluminescence.  When the MoS2 crystal is thinned to monolayer, however, a strong photoluminescence emerges, indicating an indirect to direct bandgap transition in this d-electron system. Here, for the first time, we demonstrate that in the 2D system, by alloying two materials with different band gaps (MoS2 and WS2), tunable band gap can be obtained in the 2D alloys (Mo1-xWxS2 monolayers, x = 0-1).                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reducing the Energy Band Gap of Cobalt Hydroxide Nanosheets with Silver Atoms and Enhancing Their Electrical Conductivity with Silver Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Suksomboon, Montakan; Kongsawatvoragul, Ketsuda; Duangdangchote, Salatan; Sawangphruk, Montree</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Omega</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although cobalt hydroxide (Co(OH)2) has been attracting attention in several applications, its photoelectrochem. property has not yet been fully investigated.  In this work, tuning the energy band gap of Co(OH)2 nanosheets with silver atoms and enhancing their elec. cond. with silver nanoparticles were then focused.  A Ag-doped α-Co(OH)2 thin film was successfully synthesized via an electrodeposition method.  The optical properties of the as-prepd. materials were characterized by UV-vis and fluorescence lifetime spectroscopies and further confirmed by d. functional theor. calcn.  It was found that Ag atoms between adjacent layers of Co(OH)2 can reduce its electronic band gap to 2.45 eV (α-Co(OH)2) as compared to 2.85 eV of β-Co(OH)2.  In terms of electrochem. properties, silver nanoparticles (AgNPs) can enhance the elec. cond. of Co(OH)2 nanosheets, leading to faster charge transfer reducing the internal resistance and significantly increasing the overall charge storage performance.  Interestingly, under light illumination, Ag-doped α-Co(OH)2 exhibits ca. 0.8 times lower charge storage capacity as compared to that under the dark condition.  This is because the photoelectrons can be recombined with the generated holes in the conduction band.  The charge storage mechanisms of Ag-doped α-Co(OH)2 operated under dark conditions and light irradn. were further studied and confirmed using in situ electrochem. X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS).  Overall, the in situ XAS supports the electrochem. result.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Advances in Defect-Engineered Transition Metal Dichalcogenides for Enhanced Electrocatalytic Hydrogen Evolution: Perfecting Imperfections</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tan, Zheng Hao; Kong, Xin Ying; Ng, Boon-Junn; Soo, Han Sen; Mohamed, Abdul Rahman; Chai, Siang-Piao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Omega</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1851-1863</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Switching to renewable, carbon-neutral sources of energy is urgent and crit. for climate change mitigation.  Despite how hydrogen prodn. by electrolyzing water can enable renewable energy storage, current technologies unfortunately require rare and expensive platinum group metal electrocatalysts, which limit their economic viability.  Transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) are low-cost, earth-abundant materials that possess the potential to replace platinum as the hydrogen evolution catalyst for water electrolysis, but so far, pristine TMDs are plagued by poor catalytic performances.  Defect engineering is an attractive approach to enhance the catalytic efficiency of TMDs and is not subjected to the limitations of other approaches like phase engineering and surface structure engineering.  In this mini-review, the recent progress made in defect-engineered TMDs as efficient, robust, and low-cost catalysts for water splitting is discussed.  The roles of chalcogen at. defects in engineering TMDs for improvements to the hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) are summarized.  Finally, the challenges and opportunities are highlighted of defect engineering in TMDs for electrocatalytic water splitting.  It is hoped to provide inspirations for designing the state-of-the-art catalysts for future breakthroughs in the electrocatalytic HER.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1088/1361-6528/acdf66"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dey, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium and potassium ion storage in cation substituted 2D MoWSe2: Insights into the effects of upper voltage cut-off</span>. <i>Nanotechnology</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">385401</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Few-layer MoS2 nanosheets are successfully synthesized using a simple and scalable ultrasonic exfoliation technique. The unique nanosheet architecture renders the high-rate transportation of sodium ions due to the short diffusion paths provided by ultrathin thickness and the large interlayer space within the MoS2 crystal structure (d(002) = 6.38 Å).  When applied as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, MoS2 nanosheets exhibit a high, reversible sodium storage capacity and excellent cyclability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Single- and few-layered transition metal dichalcogenides, such as MoS2 and WS2, are emerging two-dimensional materials exhibiting numerous and unusual physico-chem. properties that could be advantageous in the fabrication of unprecedented optoelectronic devices.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable synthesis of molybdenum tungsten disulfide alloy for vertically composition-controlled multilayer</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song Jeong-Gyu; Sim Sangwan; Lee Chang Wan; Choi Taejin; Jung Hanearl; Kim Youngjun; Park Jusang; Choi Hyunyong; Kim Hyungjun; Ryu Gyeong Hee; Lee Zonghoon; Lee Su Jeong; Myoung Jae-Min; Dussarrat Christian; Lansalot-Matras Clement</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">The effective synthesis of two-dimensional transition metal dichalcogenides alloy is essential for successful application in electronic and optical devices based on a tunable band gap.  Here we show a synthesis process for Mo1-xWxS2 alloy using sulfurization of super-cycle atomic layer deposition Mo1-xWxOy.  Various spectroscopic and microscopic results indicate that the synthesized Mo1-xWxS2 alloys have complete mixing of Mo and W atoms and tunable band gap by systematically controlled composition and layer number.  Based on this, we synthesize a vertically composition-controlled (VCC) Mo1-xWxS2 multilayer using five continuous super-cycles with different cycle ratios for each super-cycle.  Angle-resolved X-ray photoemission spectroscopy, Raman and ultraviolet-visible spectrophotometer results reveal that a VCC Mo1-xWxS2 multilayer has different vertical composition and broadband light absorption with strong interlayer coupling within a VCC Mo1-xWxS2 multilayer.  Further, we demonstrate that a VCC Mo1-xWxS2 multilayer photodetector generates three to four times greater photocurrent than MoS2- and WS2-based devices, owing to the broadband light absorption.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2010.07.120"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dumcenco, D.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Raman study of 2H-Mo1-xWxS2 layered mixed crystals</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dumcenco, D.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A systematic study of Mo1-xWxS2 layered mixed crystals, with 0 ≤ x ≤ 1, grown by the chem.-vapor transport method were carried out by using Raman scattering measurements.  The peaks of the 2 dominant 1st-order Raman-active modes, A1g and E2g1, and several 2nd-order bands were obsd. at 200-1000 cm-1.  The peaks corresponding to A1g mode show 1-mode type behavior while the peaks of E2g1 mode demonstrate 2-mode type behavior for the entire series.  The results can be explained from the at. displacements for each mode.  For A1g mode only S atoms vibrate and this give rise to a 1-mode type behavior for the mixed crystals.  For E2g1 mode metal atoms also vibrate as well as S atoms, the mass difference of the vibrating Mo and W cations causes the 2-mode type behavior of E2g1 mode.  The observation of largest asymmetry and broadening of A1g mode for Mo0.5W0.5S2 was attributed to random alloy scattering.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1021/nn406156b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">David, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bhandavat, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS2/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1759</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1770</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Previous studies revealed that HER activities on MoS2 could be boosted through exotic doping to introduce active centers. The simulations predict that 50% substitution of Mo by W shows the best catalytic activity because of the redn. of H adsorption free energy and facilitation of charge transfer.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use of peak fitting to ext. information from XPS data is of growing use and importance.  Due to increased instrument accessibility and reliability, the use of XPS instrumentation has significantly increased around the world.  However, the increased use has not been matched by the expertise of the new users, and the erroneous application of curve fitting has contributed to ambiguity and confusion in parts of the literature.  This guide discusses the physics and chem. involved in generating XPS spectra, describes good practices for peak fitting, and provides examples of appropriate use along with tools for avoiding mistakes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The rapid population explosion and widespread use of non-renewable energy sources have led to preoccupations such as the energy crisis, which motivates us to find alternative energy supplies and further harness their output energy through energy storage devices.  In this work, we have demonstrated hybrids incorporating MoWS2 and nanocarbon (MWCNT and rGO) as bifunctional materials, i.e., electrocatalyst and negatrode (neg. electrode), for both energy conversion and storage applications. MoS2/amorphous C microtubes (MTs) composed of heterostructured MoS2/C nanosheets were developed via a simple template method.                         cas_cit64R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">64</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical bonding boosts nano-rose-like MoS2 anchored on reduced graphene oxide for superior potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chong, Shaokun; Sun, Lan; Shu, Chengyong; Guo, Shengwu; Liu, Yongning; Wang, Wei; Liu, Hua Kun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">63</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundant and low-cost potassium resources promote potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) as promising energy storage devices, thus accelerating the investigation of ideal electrode materials to accommodate the large-size K-ions.  Here, a nano-rose-like MoS2 confined in reduced graphene oxide (MoS2@rGO) is evaluated as anode material to boost K-ion storage.  The MoS2@rGO hybrid not only features large sp. surface area for excellent electron cond. and facile K-ions diffusion, but also provides a robust three-dimension (3D) network with stable interfacial connection through strong chem. bonds (Mo-C and Mo-O-C) between MoS2 and rGO, which can alleviate the mech. stress to guarantee the structure stability during cycling.  It is also confirmed that both intercalation and conversion reaction mechanisms, based on four-electrons-transfer, play an important role in K-ions insertion/extn.  Hence, the initial capacity of 438.5 mAh·g-1 with excellent cycling stability (capacity retention of 95.0% after 200 cycles) at 100 mA g-1 and the remarkable rate capability (196.8 mAh·g-1 at 2 A g-1) among many reported anodes are achieved for MoS2@rGO.  No obvious fading at 500 mA g-1 can be obsd. over ultra-long lifespan of 1000 cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) show promise beyond Li-ion technol. in large-scale elec.-energy storage due to the abundance and low cost of potassium resources.  However, the intercalation of large-size K+ generally results in irreversible structural degrdn. and short lifespan to the hosts, representing a major obstacle.  Here, we report a new electrochem. K+-intercalation host, tungsten disulfide (WS2), which can store 0.62 K+ per formula unit with a reversible capacity of 67 mA h g-1 and well-defined voltage plateaus at an intrinsically safe av. operation potential of 0.72 V vs. K/K+.  In situ X-ray diffraction and ex situ electron microscopy revealed the underlying intercalation mechanism, a relatively small cell vol. change (37.81%), and high reversibility of this new battery chem.  Such characteristics impart WS2 with ultrahigh structural stability and a long lifespan, regardless of deep or fast charging.  WS2 achieved record-high cyclability among chalcogenides up to 600 cycles with 89.2% capacity retention at 0.3C, and over 1000 cycles with 96.3% capacity retention and an extraordinary av. Coulombic efficiency of 99.90% at 2.2C.  This intercalation electrochem. may open up new opportunities for the design of long-cycle-life and high-safety PIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref67" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201401521"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Langrock, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mignerey, A.                         cas_cit67R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">67</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced MoS2/Carbon Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Gao, Tao; Langrock, Alex; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref68" class="refNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit68" data-doi="10.1039/C8NR08511K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shangguan, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets with highly monolayer-rich structures as high-performance lithium-/sodium-ion-battery electrodes</span>. <i>Nanoscale</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1887</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1900</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets with highly monolayer-rich structures as high-performance lithium-/sodium-ion-battery electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yihui; Chang, Kun; Shangguan, Enbo; Guo, Donglei; Zhou, Wei; Hou, Yan; Tang, Hongwei; Li, Bao; Chang, Zhaorong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their low yield and easy aggregation during the electrode prepn. process, exfoliated MoS2 monolayers cannot fulfill the requirements of alkali-metal-ion battery tests.  Hence, we have developed a facile process to fabricate powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets capable of large-scale prodn. and having highly monolayer-rich structures.  This process contains two steps: liq.-phase exfoliation of the edge-rich MoS2 precursor and a freeze-drying procedure.  The proposed MoS2 precursors contain rich edge fractions that are easily exfoliated by this method, and the freeze-drying procedure can maintain the unique monolayer-rich structure of MoS2 in the powder phase.  The electrochem. evaluations of both lithium- and sodium-ion batteries reveal that the proposed powder exfoliated monolayer-rich MoS2 electrode exhibits remarkable specific capacities and stable cyclic performances.  In particular, the monolayer-rich MoS2 nanosheet electrode delivers a superior lithium-storage capacity of ∼1400 mA h g-1.  The exfoliated MoS2 nanosheet electrode can withstand over 1000 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  The mechanism reveals that these unique MoS2 nanosheets not only have a large surface area but also their inclusive monolayer structures exhibit much higher charge mobility than those of bulk MoS2.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref69"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref69" class="refNumLink">69</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit69" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c06250"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Microtubes Constructed by MoS2 Nanosheets with Enhanced Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">11</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">15577</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">15586</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit69R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">69</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Microtubes Constructed by MoS2 Nanosheets with Enhanced Sodium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Peiyuan; Sun Shumin; Zhang Yong-Hui; Zhou Liming; Fang Shaoming; Jiang Yu; Yu Yan; Cai Qiong; Liu Jian; Liu Jian; Yu Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS nano</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Emerging sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have aroused great attention in large-scale energy storage.  However, it is still a great challenge to develop suitable electrode materials due to the large radius of Na(+).  This work demonstrates a strategy to synthesize hierarchical tubular MoS2via a facial hydrothermal method with the assistance of tetramethylammonium bromide (TMAB).  The results show that sufficient amounts of TMA(+) ions are necessary to form the hierarchical tubular structures of MoS2.  The obtained tubular MoS2 displays a high diffusion coefficient of Na(+) ions, a high specific capacity of 652.5 mAh/g at the current density of 100 mA/g after 50 cycles, and a good cycling stability (94.2% of the initial capacity can be retained after 100 cycles at 1000 mA/g).  In situ XRD during the discharge/charge process displays a reversible intercalation/deintercalation of Na(+) into MoS2 layers followed by a conversion-type reaction.  Systematic analyses reveal that the enhanced electrochemical performance is attributed to its tubular hierarchical structures with the wall composed of loosely stacked nanosheets, which can provide nearly unobstructed ion transportation paths, sufficient active sites, and enough space to mitigate the effects of the volume change during the discharge/charge process.  This synthetic approach can be easily extended to other metal oxides and metal sulfides with hierarchical structures for versatile applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref70"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref70" class="refNumLink">70</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit70" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2021.138339"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ghosh, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Martha, S.                         cas_cit70R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">70</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">WS2 anode in Na and K-ion battery: Effect of upper cut-off potential on electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ghosh, Sourav; Qi, Zhimin; Wang, Haiyan; Martha, Surendra K.; Pol, Vilas G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">383</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs)-based layered anode materials are gaining attention because of their large interlayer spacing to host Na- and K-ions.  However, the capacity retention and coulombic efficiency are major obstacles for such rechargeable K-ion battery anodes.  Beside, understanding operating potential window employed during charge-discharge processes plays important role on the electrochem. performance.  The impact of operating potential window of WS2 electrodes during charge-discharge was studied in Na and K-ion battery.  WS2 nano-plates were synthesized using one step solid-state reaction under autogenic pressure at elevated temp. (RAPET) method.  The upper cut-off potential is restricted to 2.0, 2.5, and 3.0 V to understand the stability of the electrode.  The restriction of upper cut-off potential at 2.0 V, results into the capacity retention of 73% (180 mAh g-1) and 75% (250 mAh g-1) in K-ion and Na-ion batteries at the end of 50 cycles.                         cas_cit75R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">75</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of Particle Size on Mg2+ Ion Intercalation into λ-MnO2 Cathode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Wenxiang; Zhan, Xun; Luo, Binbin; Ou, Zihao; Shih, Pei-Chieh; Yao, Lehan; Pidaparthy, Saran; Patra, Arghya; An, Hyosung; Braun, Paul V.; Stephens, Ryan M.; Yang, Hong; Zuo, Jian-Min; Chen, Qian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4712-4720</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">An emergent theme in mono- and multivalent ion batteries is to utilize nanoparticles (NPs) as electrode materials based on the phenomenol. observations that their short ion diffusion length and large electrode-electrolyte interface can lead to improved ion insertion kinetics compared to their bulk counterparts.  However, the understanding of how the NP size fundamentally relates to their electrochem. behaviors (e.g., charge storage mechanism, phase transition assocd. with ion insertion) is still primitive.  Here, we employ spinel λ-MnO2 particles as a model cathode material, which have effective Mg2+ ion intercalation but with their size effect poorly understood to investigate their operating mechanism via a suite of electrochem. and structural characterizations.  We prep. two differently sized samples, the small nanoscopic λ-MnO2 particles (81 ± 25 nm) and big micron-sized ones (814 ± 207 nm) via postsynthesis size-selection.  Anal. of the charge storage mechanisms shows that the stored charge from Mg2+ ion intercalation dominates in both systems and is ∼10 times higher in small particles than that in the big ones.  From both X-ray diffraction and at.-resoln. scanning transmission electron microscopy imaging, we reveal a fundamental difference in phase transition of the differently sized particles during Mg2+ ion intercalation: the small NPs undergo a solid-soln.-like phase transition which minimizes lattice mismatch and energy penalty for accommodating new phases, whereas the big particles follow conventional multiphase transformation.  We show that this pathway difference is related to the improved electrochem. performance (e.g., rate capability, cycling performance) of small particles over the big ones which provides important insights in encoding within the particle dimension, i.e., the single-phase transition pathway in high-performance electrode materials for multivalent ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref76"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref76" class="refNumLink">76</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit76" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601283"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cook, J.                         cas_cit77R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">77</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO2 (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Lim, James; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14925-14931</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref78"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref78" class="refNumLink">78</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit78" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01211J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A self-assembled 3D urchin-like Ti0.8Sn0.2O2–rGO hybrid nanostructure as an anode material for high-rate and long cycle life Li-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. Zn-ion batteries (ZIBs) are considered very promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries.  However, the low reversibility and slow diffusion of zinc ions in the pos. electrode limit their com. applications.  Herein, we successfully prepd. the metallic 1T phase of MoS2 (1T-MoS2) with a nano interlayer spacing of 1.025 nm through a simple one-step hydrothermal method, and used it as a cathode in ZIBs.  By adjusting the hydrothermal temp., the crystallinity and Zn2+ storage capacity of MoS2 as a cathode for ZIBs are effectively improved.  MoS2 had the most favorable structure when the hydrothermal temp. was 200°C, such as larger layer spacing and more lattice distortion.  When employed as a cathode, 200-MoS2 exhibited a considerable specific capacity of 125 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 2 A g-1 and high capacity retention of 100% after 500 cycles.  This strategy provides a new option for improving the performance of the layered structure as an aq. zinc ion battery.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref80"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref80" class="refNumLink">80</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit80" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201806752"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Long Cycle Life Lithium Metal Batteries Enabled with Upright Lithium Anode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit81R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">81</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Thermodynamic and mass transport properties of "lithium aluminide"</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, C. John; Boukamp, B. A.; Huggins, R. A.; Weppner, W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1979</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">126</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2258-66</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The compositional variations of the thermodn. and mass transport properties of the β phase "LiAl" in the system were investigated at 415° to 600°.  At 415° the emf. of the single phase "LiAl" lies between 300 and 70 mV relative to pure Li and this corresponds to a Li activity increasing from 0.0063 to 0.31 over the phase stability range from 46.8 to 55.0 at. % Li.  At the ideal stoichiometry, the std. Gibbs free energy of formation of "LiAl" is -29.2 kJ/mol at 415° and the corresponding enthalpy and entropy are -43.3 and -20.6 J/mol K, resp.  Two different electrochem. transient techniques were used to measure the chem. diffusion coeff. in "LiAl" as a function of the stoichiometry; the exptl. results obtained are in good agreement.  On the Li deficient side of ideal stoichiometry, the chem. diffusion coeff. increases with decreasing Li concn., becoming about 10-4 cm2/s near the phase boundary.  On the other hand, it is compn. independent on the Li excess side of "LiAl," varying with temp. from 2.4 × 10-6 cm2/s at 415° to 1.8 × 10-5 cm2/s at 600°.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref82"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref82" class="refNumLink">82</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit82" data-doi="10.1002/celc.202001486"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bashir, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage Performance of a 2D MoS2 Anode Material Coated on Carbon Nanotubes</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">5</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">903</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">910</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit82R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">82</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage Performance of a 2D MoS2 Anode Material Coated on Carbon Nanotubes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wanying; Bashir, Tariq; Wang, Jiaqi; Zhou, Shaowen; Yang, Shiqi; Zhao, Jianqing; Gao, Lijun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">903-910</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) is considered a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, it suffers from poor kinetics and rapid capacity decay.  In this work, a coaxial heterostructure composed of MoS2 nanosheets coated on carbon nanotubes (CNTs) is reported, where the MoS2 layers are less stacked at the surface of the CNTs substrate with an enhanced interlayer spacing, which is prepd. through a simple one-pot hydrothermal prepn.  The MoS2@CNTs composite material is proven to have superior rate performance as an anode material for SIBs, which delivers 508, 418, 359, 305, 258, and 183 mAh/g at current densities of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A/g, resp., together with excellent cycling stability to retain 360 mAh/g after 400 cycles at 0.5 A/g, owing to the robust combination of MoS2 and CNT components.  This work offers a way to synthesize heterostructured composite materials with great performance superiority for large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref83"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref83" class="refNumLink">83</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit83" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.152821"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A novel MoS2@C framework architecture composites with three-dimensional cross-linked porous carbon supporting MoS2 nanosheets for sodium storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit83R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">83</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A novel MoS2@C framework architecture composites with three-dimensional cross-linked porous carbon supporting MoS2 nanosheets for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xia; Ma, Ting; Fang, Tao; Gao, Yunzhi; Gao, Shuai; Wang, Wenwen; Liao, Lixia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">818</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">152821</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0925-8388</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The exploration of appropriate electrode materials for high-performance Na-ion batteries (SIBs) is deemed to a crit. technol. challenge to satisfy the ever-increasing demand for energy storage and conversion market.  Herein, Mo sulfide (MoS2) nanosheets anchored on porous C (MoS2@C) were synthesized via a facile and controllable method.  The novel three-dimensional (3D) honeycomb-like hierarchical structure is capable of offering reduced ion diffusion pathways, buffering vol. expansion, as well as stabilizing interface.  Benefiting from the 3-dimensional ion diffusion channels formed by this unique architecture, a high intercalation pseudocapacitance (77% at the scan rate of 1.5 mV s-1) is achieved, which is responsible for the good rate capability (∼372 and 225 mAh g-1 at 0.05 and 2 A g-1, resp.).  Also, the composites deliver the long cycle performance (233 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 over 200 cycles) compared with the pristine MoS2 electrode.  Also, 3-dimensional roughness reconstruction of the MoS2@C electrode well reveals the integrity of the hierarchical structure after Na+ insertion.  The authors' work paves a new way for the application of MoS2@C and opens up new opportunities for the broader design of SIBs anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref84"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref84" class="refNumLink">84</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit84" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b14742"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering Hollow Porous Carbon-Sphere-Confined MoS2 with Expanded (002) Planes for Boosting Potassium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The current lithium-ion battery (LIB) electrode fabrication process relies heavily on the wet coating process, which uses the environmentally harmful and toxic N-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP) solvent.  In addn. to being unsustainable, the use of this expensive org. solvent substantially increases the cost of battery prodn., as it needs to be dried and recycled throughout the manufg. process.  Herein, we report an industrially viable and sustainable dry press-coating process that uses the combination of multiwalled carbon nanotubes (MWNTs) and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) as a dry powder composite and etched Al foil as a current collector.  Notably, the mech. strength and performance of the fabricated LiNi0.7Co0.1Mn0.2O2 (NCM712) dry press-coated electrodes (DPCEs) far exceed those of conventional slurry-coated electrodes (SCEs) and give rise to high loading (100 mg cm-2, 17.6 mAh cm-2) with impressive specific energy and volumetric energy d. of 360 Wh kg-1 and 701 Wh L-1, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/s41565-020-0657-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, D. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From nanoscale interface characterization to sustainable energy storage using all-solid-state batteries</span>. <i>Nat.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The recent discovery of highly conductive solid-state electrolytes (SSEs) has led to tremendous progress in the development of all-solid-state batteries (ASSBs).  Though promising, they still face barriers that limit their practical application, such as poor interfacial stability, scalability challenges and prodn. safety.  Addnl., efforts to develop sustainable manufg. of lithium ion batteries are still lacking, with no prevailing strategy developed yet to handle recyclability of ASSBs.  To date, most SSE research has been largely focused on the discovery of novel electrolytes.  Recent review articles have extensively examd. a broad spectrum of these SSEs using evaluation factors such as cond. and chem. stability.  Recognizing this, in this Review we seek to evaluate SSEs beyond conventional factors and offer a perspective on various bulk, interface and nanoscale phenomena that require urgent attention within the scientific community.  We provide a realistic assessment of the current state-of-the-art characterization techniques and evaluate future full cell ASSB prototyping strategies.  We hope to offer rational solns. to overcome some major fundamental obstacles faced by the ASSB community, as well as potential strategies toward a sustainable ASSB recycling model.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.aav7412"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Approaching high-performance potassium-ion batteries via advanced design strategies and engineering</span>. <i>Sci. Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">5</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">eaav7412</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.mattod.2021.03.015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges and future perspectives on sodium and potassium ion batteries for grid-scale energy storage</span>. <i>Mater. Today</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>50</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">400</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">417</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.mattod.2021.03.015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Challenges and future perspectives on sodium and potassium ion batteries for grid-scale energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenchao; Lu, Jun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">400-417</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The energy crisis and environmental pollution require the advancement of large-scale energy storage techniques.  Among the various commercialized technologies, batteries have attracted enormous attention due to their relatively high energy d. and long cycle life.  Nevertheless, the limited supply and uneven distribution of lithium minerals, as well as their high cost, has greatly hindered the application of lithium-ion batteries in large-scale energy storage.  Therefore, building next-generation alternative rechargeable batteries that feature low cost, long service life, and high safety is of the utmost importance.  Over the past several years, we have witnessed many successful research outcomes for sodium and potassium ion batteries (SIBs and PIBs) in regard to electrode and electrolyte materials.  In this Perspective, we summarize the current developments on SIBs/PIBs and their challenges when facing practical applications, including their cost, energy d., ion diffusivity in solids/electrolytes/interphases, cycle life, and safety concerns.  Furthermore, we provide an overview of strategies to overcome the remaining challenges for achieving better electrochem. performance.  Finally, we outline several possible directions for the future development of these two battery chemistries, with the hope of aiding the transition from the lab. to next-generation practical applications for SIBs/PIBs batteries in grid-scale energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1038/35104644"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive low-cost alternative to Li-ion batteries.  Although graphite is used as the neg. electrode in conventional Li-ion batteries, attempts to use it in Na-ion batteries have been hampered by the inability of Na to form graphite intercalation compds. (GICs) under moderate conditions.  It is generally considered that this is due to the size mismatch between Na and the graphite interlayer spacings, but here we show with detailed first-principles calcns. of Li, Na, K, Rb, and Cs GICs that the major reason is the change in chem. bonding between alkali metal (AM) ion and C atoms. van der Waals correction terms are introduced to better reproduce the layered graphite structure, and calcd. formation energies of GICs AMC6, where AM = Li, Na, K, Rb, and Cs, are found to become less neg. (less stable) as ion size decreases from Cs to Na as a result of weakening ionic bonding, until the formation energy of NaC6 becomes pos.  The much smaller Li ion represents an exception to this trend, as its bonds with C atoms contain a covalent component, resulting in a neg. formation energy.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Expanded graphite (EG) has been shown to be able to store a significant amt. of sodium ions.  Understanding the alkali metal ion storage in EG is of importance for improving EG electrode performance.  In this work, the effect of interlayer distance of pure EG on sodium ion storage was investigated using the d. functional theory calcn. method.  EG structure models with interlayer distances ranging from 3.4 Å to 10.0 Å were simulated.  It was found that EG can store a fairly large amt. of sodium ions through an intercalation mechanism without any contributions from the co-intercalation mechanism or adsorption mechanism if the interlayer distance is larger than 4.4 Å and smaller than 6.0 Å.  It was also found that an interlayer distance of 6.0 Å gives strong binding energy of sodium ions with EG forming thermodynamically stable sodium-graphite intercalation compd. (Na-GIC).  However, when the interlayer distance becomes larger than 6.0 Å, the binding energy between sodium ions and EG becomes weaker.  Computational results have also shown that the enthalpy of formation of the Na-GIC of EG is energetically more favorable when the interlayer distance is increased.  An optimal d-spacing of EG for sodium ion storage was identified in this work.  These findings provide atomistic insights into sodium ion storage in EG, providing guidelines for the design of graphite-based anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.20517/energymater.2023.79"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Trano, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Versaci, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Castellino, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fontana, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fagiolari, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Francia, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bella, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exploring nature-behaviour relationship of carbon black materials for potassium-ion battery electrodes</span>. <i>Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">400008</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The org. metal-ion battery field remains challenged by the lack of high-voltage alkali-cation reservoir cathode materials.  Whereas a few recent breakthroughs provided valuable solns. for Li-ion storage, Na-ion and K-ion org. reservoirs with high voltage and ambient stability remain elusive.  Herein, we show that the versatile benzene-1,2,4,5-tetrayltetrakis methylsulfonyl-amide (PTtSA) tetra-anionic framework displays universal performance for alkali cation storage.  The new synthesized Na4-PTtSA and K4-PTtSA phases reversibly exchange two Na+ or K+ equiv. per formula unit at redox potentials of 2.5 V vs Na+/Na and 2.6 V vs K+/K, resp.  A singular comparative anal. of Li-, Na-, and K-ion phases discloses the impact of the alkali cation on the physicochem. properties, with direct impact on the electrochem. of the materials.  This work not only offers guidance and principles to tune the redox properties of org. redox materials via spectator cations but also highlights the versatility of org. materials for alkali cation storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1038/s41598-024-53154-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tanibata, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nonaka, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Makino, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takeda, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakayama, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chloride electrode composed of ubiquitous elements for high-energy-density all-solid-state sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  High-voltage potassium-based batteries are promising alternatives for lithium-ion batteries as next-generation energy storage devices.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium batteries show interesting peculiarities as large-scale energy storage systems and, in this scenario, the formulation of polymer electrolytes obtained from sustainable resources or waste-derived products represents a milestone activity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Humid hydrophobic ionic liqs.-widely used as electrolytes-have narrowed electrochem. windows due to the involvement of water, absorbed on the electrode surface, in electrolysis.  In this work, we performed mol. dynamics simulations to explore effects of adding Li salt in humid ionic liqs. on the water adsorbed on the electrode surface.  Results reveal that most of the water mols. are pushed away from both cathode and anode, by adding salt.  The water remaining on the electrode is almost bound with Li+, having significantly lowered activity.  The Li+-bonding and re-arrangement of the surface-adsorbed water both facilitate the inhibition of water electrolysis, and thus prevent the redn. of electrochem. windows of humid hydrophobic ionic liqs.  This finding is testified by cyclic voltammetry measurements where salt-in-humid ionic liqs. exhibit enlarged electrochem. windows.  Our work provides the underlying mechanism and a simple but practical approach for protection of humid ionic liqs. from electrochem. performance degrdn.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1073/pnas.2314408120"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemical and spatial dual-confinement engineering for stable Na-S batteries with approximately 100% capacity retention</span>. <i>Proc.                         rightTab-cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transition metal dichalcogenides for alkali metal ion batteries: engineering strategies at the atomic level</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Biao; Chao, Dongliang; Liu, Enzuo; Jaroniec, Mietek; Zhao, Naiqin; Qiao, Shi-Zhang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  In the past few decades, great effort has been made toward the prepn. and development of advanced transition metal dichalcogenide (TMD) materials for anodes of alkali metal ion batteries (AMIBs).  However, their electrochem. performance is still severely impaired by structural aggregation and fracture during the conversion reaction.  To address these issues, various methodologies for the fabrication of hierarchical and hybrid nanostructures, with optimization of materials and electrodes, have been fully investigated and reviewed.  As regards tuning the TMD-based materials, extensive efforts have been undertaken toward optimization of their intrinsic structure at the at. level, including surface defects, interlayer spacing expansion, phase control, alloying, and heteroatom doping.  However, the design strategies and methods to manipulate the intrinsic structures and electrochem. mechanisms in AMIBs have not been fully summarized.  This review provides a well-timed and crit. appraisal of recent advances in the engineering of TMDs at the at. level for AMIBs, by combining computational and exptl. approaches.  The correlation between these strategies and electrochem. performance is highlighted.  The challenges and opportunities in this research field are also outlined.  We expect that this review would be beneficial for improving the overall knowledge on the charge storage mechanisms in TMDs and for pointing out the importance of intrinsic structure engineering for enhancing the performance of TMDs in energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501937"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cook, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As a two-dimensional layered material, SnS is considered a promising candidate anode material for sodium storage due to its high theor. capacity (1022 mA h g-1) and large interlayer spacing (4.33 Å).  However, its application is hindered by its large vol. expansion and low electronic cond.  Herein, a unique MoS2/SnS@C hollow hierarchical nanotube with self-supporting structure was synthesized through a facile solvothermal reaction.  The results indicate that the hollow nanotube structure can support the material structure and provide a large sodium-ion migration channel.  In addn., the heterojunction that formed between SnS and MoS2 can effectively reduce the kinetic barrier of sodium-ion diffusion.  Furthermore, the hollow hierarchical nanotube can effectively alleviate the radial and hoop stresses of the SnS sodiation process, inhibit the vol. expansion of the material, and increase the capacitance contribution ratio of the material at a high rate.  The MoS2/SnS@C composites used as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) delivered excellent rate and cycle performance.  The discharge capacity was about 325 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 15 A g-1, and it remained at about 292 mA h g-1 after 2000 cycles at 5 A g-1 c.d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201401205"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) exhibit immense potential as lithium/ sodium-ion electrode materials owing to their sandwich-like layered structures.  To optimize their lithium/sodium-storage performance, two issues should be addressed: fundamentally understanding the chem. reaction occurring in TMD electrodes and developing novel TMDs.  In this study, WSe2 hexagonal nanoplates were synthesized as lithium/sodium-ion battery (LIB/SIB) electrode materials.  For LIBs, the WSe2-nanoplate electrodes achieved a stable reversible capacity and a high rate capability, as well as an ultralong cycle life of up to 1,500 cycles at 1,000 mA·g-1.  Most importantly, in situ Raman spectroscopy, ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD), transmission electron microscopy, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy measurements performed during the discharge-charge process clearly verified the reversible conversion mechanism, which can be summarized as follows: WSe2 + 4Li+ + 4e- ↔ W + 2Li2Se.  The WSe2 nanoplates also exhibited excellent cycling performance and a high rate capability as SIB electrodes.  Ex situ XRD and Raman spectroscopy results demonstrate that WSe2 reacted with Na+ more easily and thoroughly than with Li+ and converted to Na2Se and tungsten in the 1st sodiated state.  The subsequent charging reaction can be expressed as Na2Se → Se + 2Na+ + 2e-, which differs from the traditional conversion mechanism for LIBs.  To our knowledge, this is the first systematic exploration of the lithium/sodium-storage performance of WSe2 and the mechanism involved.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although cobalt hydroxide (Co(OH)2) has been attracting attention in several applications, its photoelectrochem. property has not yet been fully investigated. The optical properties of the as-prepd. materials were characterized by UV-vis and fluorescence lifetime spectroscopies and further confirmed by d. functional theor. calcn.
